# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes Scheduler Plugin Framework Architecture

## Your Task

A new Kubernetes contributor wants to understand the scheduler plugin framework architecture. Find the key Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the scheduling framework: 1. The framework interface definitions (Plugin, FilterPlugin, ScorePlugin, BindPlugin, etc. in pkg/scheduler/framework/). 2. The ScheduleOne orchestration function that drives the scheduling cycle for a single pod. 3. The top-level Scheduler struct and its Run method. 4. The frameworkImpl runtime that invokes plugins (RunFilterPlugins, RunScorePlugins). 5. The plugin registry and the NewInTreeRegistry that registers all built-in plugins. Report each file path and key symbols.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the onboarding domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully created the `answer.json` file with a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes scheduler plugin framework architecture. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Located:

### 1. **Framework Interface Definitions** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go`)
- `Plugin` (base interface for all plugins at line 443)
- `FilterPlugin` (line 540): Filters nodes that cannot run a pod
- `ScorePlugin` (line 607): Ranks filtered nodes
- `BindPlugin` (line 673): Binds pod to node
- Plus 10 more extension point interfaces (PreFilter, PostFilter, PreScore, Reserve, PreBind, PostBind, Permit, QueueSort, PreEnqueue, EnqueueExtensions)

### 2. **Top-Level Scheduler Struct** (`pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go`)
- `Scheduler` struct (line 66): Manages cache, scheduling queue, and profiles
- `Run()` method (line 464): Starts the scheduling loop, launching ScheduleOne in a dedicated goroutine

### 3. **ScheduleOne Orchestration** (`pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go`)
- `ScheduleOne()` function (line 65): Drives the complete scheduling workflow for a single pod

### 4. **Framework Runtime** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go`)
- `frameworkImpl` struct (line 52): Initializes and runs plugins
- `RunFilterPlugins()` method (line 872): Executes filter plugins sequentially
- `RunScorePlugins()` method (line 1112): Executes score plugins in parallel

### 5. **Plugin Registry** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go`)
- `NewInTreeRegistry()` function (line 47): Registers all built-in plugins (18 plugins including NodeAffinity, TaintToleration, PodTopologySpread, VolumeBinding, etc.)

The answer file includes the execution chain: **Run() → ScheduleOne() → RunFilterPlugins() → RunScorePlugins()**, showing how control flows through the scheduler framework.

A plugin may use this data to update internal\n586: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\n587: type PreScorePlugin interface {\n588: \tPlugin\n589: \t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n590: \t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n591: \t// the pod will be rejected\n592: \t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n593: \t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n594: \tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n595: }\n596: \n597: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\n598: type ScoreExtensions interface {\n599: \t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n600: \t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n601: \t// a success status.\n602: \tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n603: }\n604: \n605: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n606: // nodes that passed the filtering phase.\n607: type ScorePlugin interface {\n608: \tPlugin\n609: \t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\n610: \t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\n611: \t// the pod will be rejected.\n612: \tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\n613: \n614: \t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n615: \tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\n616: }\n617: \n618: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n619: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n620: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n621: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n622: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n623: // rejection of the pod.\n624: type ReservePlugin interface {\n625: \tPlugin\n626: \t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n627: \t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\n628: \t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\n629: \tReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n630: \t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\n631: \t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\n632: \t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\n633: \t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\n634: \t// method for the same plugin was not called.\n635: \tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n636: }\n637: \n638: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreBind\" plugins.\n639: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\n640: type PreBindPlugin interface {\n641: \tPlugin\n642: \t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\n643: \t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\n644: \tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n645: }\n646: \n647: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PostBind\" plugins.\n648: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\n649: type PostBindPlugin interface {\n650: \tPlugin\n651: \t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\n652: \t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\n653: \t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\n654: \t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\n655: \tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n656: }\n657: \n658: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Permit\" plugins.\n659: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\n660: type PermitPlugin interface {\n661: \tPlugin\n662: \t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\n663: \t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n664: \t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n665: \t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n666: \t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \"wait\", the framework will wait only\n667: \t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\n668: \tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\n669: }\n670: \n671: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Bind\" plugins. Bind\n672: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\n673: type BindPlugin interface {\n674: \tPlugin\n675: \t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n676: \t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n677: \t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\n678: \t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\n679: \t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\n680: \t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\n681: \tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n682: }\n683: \n684: // Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\n685: // Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\n686: type Framework interface {\n687: \tHandle\n688: \n689: \t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\n690: \tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\n691: \n692: \t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\n693: \tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\n694: \n695: \t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\n696: \tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\n697: \n698: \t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. It returns\n699: \t// *Status and its code is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\n700: \t// anything but Success. If a non-success status is returned, then the scheduling\n701: ",

Runs PreScore and Score plugins to rank nodes\\n6. Handles binding, permitting, and other post-score phases\\nThis is serialized on the scheduling algorithm's host fitting.\\n\\n**Framework Runtime (pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go, line 52):**\\nframeworkImpl is the component responsible for initializing and running scheduler plugins. Iterates through filterPlugins and returns status on first failure.\\n- RunScorePlugins (line 1112): Runs all Score plugins in parallel across nodes. Each plugin scores all nodes, then results are normalized and aggregated.\\n\\nBoth methods handle metrics recording, logging at different verbosity levels, and check for skipped plugins via CycleState.\\n\\n**Plugin Registry (pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/registry.go, line 47):**\\nNewInTreeRegistry() builds the registry with all in-tree plugins, returning runtime.Registry (line 47). The registry can be extended with out-of-tree plugins via WithFrameworkOutOfTreeRegistry option.\\n\\n**Execution Chain:**\\nScheduler.Run() -> ScheduleOne() -> framework.RunFilterPlugins() -> framework.RunScorePlugins() -> binding phase plugins.
